## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, the task most naturally fits thermoelastic/thermoplastic constitutive relations where stress depends on mechanical strain and temperature-driven modulus/strength changes (and possibly thermal strain offsets).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear softening/stiffening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E varies approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential form): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (empirical E(T) for wider ranges)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain subtraction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion reduces mechanical strain; c1 ~ alpha, c0 ~ E)
- Thermoelastic stress with T-dependent thermal expansion: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - (c1 + c2 * T) * (T - c3)) (alpha(T) varying with temperature)
- Quadratic nonlinearity (Landau-type / weakly nonlinear elasticity): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon^2 (moderate strains, polynomial constitutive fit)
- Cubic nonlinearity (higher-order elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^2 + c2 * epsilon^3 (nonlinear elastic response in small-to-moderate strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit; can be rearranged for sigma): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma^(c2) with c0, c1 possibly functions of T (elastic + nonlinear plastic strain representation)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent strength scale: sigma = c0 * (c1 + c2 * T) * (c3 + epsilon)^(c4) (work hardening with thermal softening/stiffening through the prefactor)
- Voce-type saturation hardening (strain hardening saturates): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (approach to a saturation stress; temperature shifts levels)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic with linear hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon for epsilon <= c1; sigma = c0 * c1 + c2 * (epsilon - c1) for epsilon > c1 (yield then hardening; c0,c2 may depend on T)
- Johnson–Cook-like (without strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon^(c2)) * (c3 + c4 * T)^(c5) (empirical plastic flow stress capturing strain hardening and thermal softening via a multiplicative T-factor)
- Entropic (rubber-like) elasticity scaling: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (polymer network elasticity where modulus is proportional to absolute temperature)
- Sigmoidal transition in stiffness/strength around a characteristic temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 / (1 + exp(c2 * (T - c3)))) * epsilon (smooth glass-transition-like drop in modulus with T)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion effects often appear as an effective strain shift: sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T - T0)), so subtracting a T-dependent offset from epsilon is physically meaningful.
- Elastic modulus typically decreases with temperature for many metals/ceramics; this suggests multiplicative forms like sigma = E(T)*epsilon with E(T) monotone in T (linear or exponential fits).
- Work hardening commonly follows a power law in strain (epsilon^n) or saturates (1 - exp(-k*epsilon)); adding T-dependence to the prefactor captures thermal softening.
- Yield/flow stress often drops with temperature, motivating multiplicative softening factors in T (e.g., (c0 + c1*T)^(c2) or logistic-in-T transitions).
- If the material shows a regime change (elastic to plastic) or a phase/transition temperature, piecewise or smoothly switched (logistic) models in epsilon or T are typical.
- Rubbery/entropic elasticity implies stress proportional to absolute temperature at fixed strain, so sigma ∝ T*epsilon is a recognizable signature.
- Nonlinear elastic responses at moderate strain are often well-captured by low-order polynomials in epsilon (quadratic/cubic) with coefficients that vary with T.
- When temperature primarily rescales stiffness rather than changing curve shape, prefer separable multiplicative structure sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) over fully coupled polynomials.

Structure desc      : Additive composition of bilinear T*ε, constant, a decaying exp(-k|ε|), a one-sided exponential exp(c5ε), and a sinusoid in ε. ε appears in three nonlinear terms (Abs-exp, signed exp, sine), while T only multiplies ε. The Abs-exp term is tiny (c2≈6.75 with c3≈-5.90), but the signed exponential has large amplitude c4≈531 and decays for positive ε (c5≈-2.16) while exploding for negative ε, suggesting potential extrapolation instability; the sine amplitude is very large (c6≈1092). Approximately f≈0.631Tε+24+6.75e^{−5.90|ε|}+531e^{−2.16ε}+1092·sin(5.743+0.813ε).
